Accidents Do Not Persist: The Ash'ari View
Al-Iji states the Ash'ari doctrine that accidents are non-enduring.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine that accidents are non-enduring and require constant recreation at each moment.

Core Idea
All accidents are new every moment; none lasts two instants.

This lesson introduces a core Ash'ari principle about the nature of accidents. According to al-Ash'ari and his verifying followers, no accident endures for two consecutive moments. Instead, accidents are continuously passing away and being renewed, which underpins their occasionalist worldview.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note that this is a concise doctrinal statement.
The passage is short but foundational for Ash'ari atomism.
2
Understand the claim
The key claim is that accidents do not 'remain' (لا يبقى) for two moments. Ask yourself: what does 'remaining' mean here? It means persisting identically across time.
Accidents are like properties (color, sound) that inhere in substances.
3
Grasp the implication
Since accidents do not endure, they must be recreated by God at each moment. This leads to constant renewal (التجدد) and passing away (التقصي).
This contrasts with the view that some accidents are stable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ المقصد السابع : أن العرض لا يبقي زمانين ] وذهب الشيخ الأشعري ومتبعوه من محققي الأشاعرة إلى أن العرض لا يبقي زمانين فالأعراض جملتها غير باقية عندهم بل هي على التقصي والتجدد ينقضي
[ The seventh objective: That the accident does not remain for two moments ] And al-Ash'ari and his followers among the verifying Ash'aris went to [the position] that the accident does not remain for two moments, so all accidents according to them are non-enduring; rather they are in a state of passing away and renewal, they pass away.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh objective, which is a simple doctrinal statement. It asserts the Ash'ari position that no accident (عرض) persists for two consecutive moments of time. According to al-Ash'ari and the verifying Ash'aris, all accidents are continuously passing away and being replaced; they do not endure. This is a fundamental principle of Ash'ari atomism: accidents are created anew at every moment, which underpins their occasionalist ontology.

Key Terms
العرض
البقاء
الزمان
التجدد
التقصي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some accidents, like motion or color, might persist for a while.
Correction: The Ash'ari view, as stated here, holds that no accident endures for even two moments; all are constantly recreated.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh objective, what is the view of al-Ash'ari and his followers regarding accidents?
A) Accidents persist for two moments.
B) Accidents are eternal.
C) Accidents do not remain for two moments and are constantly renewed.
D) Accidents persist only in the mind.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari and his followers maintain that accidents do not endure for two moments; they are perpetually passing away and being renewed by God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every accident in your life—every breath, every heartbeat, every thought—is created anew by God each moment, what does that imply about your own sense of control and self-reliance? How should this change the way you begin each day?
?
The Ash'ari view teaches that nothing in the created world—not even the sound of your voice—lasts for two moments. When you sin, that sin is a non-enduring accident. Does that diminish the guilt of sin? Or does it magnify the fact that God chooses to recreate that sin in you each moment? Reflect on the weight of each moment in light of this.
?
If your very existence is sustained by God's continuous creation, what does that mean for your gratitude? How would you live differently today knowing that without God's constant renewal, you would cease to be? What specific aspect of your life have you taken for granted that is actually being recreated right now?

Al-Nazzam's Doctrine: Body as Aggregate of Accidents
Al-Nazzam states his view that the body is a collection of accidents, and explains the implication for renewal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nazzam's view that the body is a collection of accidents and how this leads to the conclusion that accident renewal entails body renewal.

Core Idea
For al-Nazzam, the body is nothing but aggregated accidents; thus if accidents renew, the body renews.

Al-Nazzam held a unique view that the body is composed solely of aggregated accidents. This lesson introduces his doctrine and explains why he believed that the renewal of accidents necessarily implies the renewal of the body. The passage also distinguishes between different types of accidents and clarifies what constitutes the body's reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Nazzam's view is presented as a lemma from al-Mawaqif.
2
Identify al-Nazzam's definition of body
The passage states that the body is a collection of accidents that remain accidental but become bodies through aggregation. Find the exact wording.
This is the foundation of his doctrine.
3
Understand the implication of accident renewal
If the body is nothing but accidents, then the renewal of accidents necessarily renews the body. Ask yourself: Is this a valid conclusion?
This leads to the need for proof extension discussed later.
4
Notice the distinction among accidents
The passage clarifies that some things (modes, beliefs) are accidents with no role in the body's reality, while others (colors, tastes) are considered subtle bodies by al-Nazzam. Reflect on why this distinction matters.
This shows the complexity of al-Nazzam's category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (يلزم من تجدد الأعراض تجدد (الأجسام لأنَّ المستفاد من قوله أن الجسم مجموع أعراض مجتمعة أنها باقية على عروضيتها وصارت بسبب الاجتماع أجساماً فيكون تجددها موجباً لتجددها هذا لكن في شرح التجريد أن المذكور في كتب المعتزلة أن مثل الأكوان والاعتقادات والآلام واللذات وما أشبه ذلك أعراض لا دخل لها في حقيقة الجسم وفاقاً وأما الألوان والطعوم والروائح والأصوات والكيفيات الملموسة من الحرارة والبرودة وغيرهما فعن النظام جواهر بل أجسام حيث صرح بأنَّ كلاً من ذلك لطيف مركب من جواهر مجتمعة ثم إنَّ تلك الأجسام اللطيفة إذا اجتمعت وتداخلت صارت الجسم الكثيف الذي هو الجماد . :قوله : ( بلا حاجة إلى طرد الدليل لعل المراد من طرد الدليل إجراؤها في جزئي من جزئيات ما أقيم عليه لخفاء فيه كما سيجيء في التنبيه المذكور في المقصد الثالث الأجسام باقية حيث قال : الدليل لما قام في الأعراض طرده النظام في الأجسام فقال بعدم بقائها أيضا قال الآمدي : وذلك لأنه مبني على أصله وهو أنَّ الجوهر مركب من الأعراض انتهى فعلى هذا لزوم تجدد الأجسام من تجدد الأعراض لا ينفي الاحتياج إلى الطرد. قوله : ( وإنما يحتاج إليه إذا كانت الأجسام عنده مركبة من الجواهر الأفراد فيه بحث لأن تركب الجسم من الجواهر الأفراد الغير المتناهية وإن كان مشهوراً من مذهبه إلا أن الجوهر الفرد بل الجوهر مطلقاً مركب عنده من محض الأعراض المجتمعة كما سيجيء في موقف الجوهر فالأجزاء الغير المتناهية عنده جواهر غير متناهية مركب كل منها من الأعراض المجتمعة ولا فرق في الاحتياج المذكور وعدمه بين القولين لأن مبنى نفي الاحتياج على تقدير كون الجسم مجموع الأعراض المجتمعة هو أنَّ المركب من محض الأعراض يلزم أن يكون عرضاً كما يشهد به البديهة وإن كان جوهراً عند النظام فالدليل الدال على تجدد الأعراض دال على تجدد الجسم لاندراجه فيها فلا احتياج إلى طرد الدليل فيه كما لا احتياج إلى طرده في خصوصيات الأعراض وهذا اللزوم لا يختلف على القولين كما لا يخفى على المتأمل اللهم إلا أن يثبت عنه نقل آخر وهو القول بالجزء على نحو ما قال به سائر المتكلمين، وإن لم يذكره المصنف وبما ذكرنا يظهر أن عدم الاحتياج إلى طرد الدليل على ما يشهد به البديهة لا على ما ادعاه النظام من جوهرية مذهبه
His statement: (It follows from the renewal of accidents the renewal of bodies) because what is understood from his statement that the body is a collection of accidents is that they (the accidents) remain upon their accidentally and by aggregation become bodies, so their renewal necessitates their renewal. However, in Sharh al-Tajrid it is mentioned that what is recorded in the books of the Mu'tazila is that things like modes (akwan), beliefs, pains, pleasures, and the like are accidents that have no entry in the reality of the body by agreement. As for colors, tastes, smells, sounds, and tangible qualities like heat and cold and others, according to al-Nazzam they are substances (jawahir) rather bodies (ajsam), for he explicitly stated that each of these is a subtle thing composed of aggregated substances, and then those subtle bodies when they aggregate and interpenetrate become the dense body which is the inanimate. His statement: (without need to extend the proof (sard al-dalil)) perhaps the meaning of 'extending the proof' is applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was established, due to obscurity therein, as will come in the notice mentioned in the third objective: bodies are enduring. For he said: The proof when it was established for accidents, al-Nazzam extended it to bodies and said they also do not endure. Al-Amidi said: That is because it is built upon his principle – that the substance (jawhar) is composed of accidents. End of quote. On this basis, the necessity of bodies' renewal from the renewal of accidents does not negate the need for extending the proof. His statement: (And it is only needed if bodies in his view are composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad).) There is discussion in it, because composition of the body from infinite individual atoms – though it is well-known from his doctrine – nevertheless the individual atom, nay substance absolutely, is in his view composed of mere aggregated accidents, as will come in the station of substance. So the infinite parts are in his view infinite substances each composed of aggregated accidents. There is no difference between the two views concerning the aforementioned need or lack thereof, because the basis for negating the need on the assumption that the body is a collection of aggregated accidents is that a composite of mere accidents necessarily is an accident, as intuition (badiha) testifies, even if it is a substance according to al-Nazzam. So the proof indicating the renewal of accidents indicates the renewal of the body because it falls under them, so there is no need to extend the proof to it, just as there is no need to extend it to specifics of accidents. And this implication does not differ between the two views, as is not hidden from the contemplator. Unless there is established from him another transmitted statement – namely the saying of the part (al-juz') in the manner spoken by the rest of the theologians, even if the author did not mention it. And by what we have mentioned it becomes apparent that the lack of need for extending the proof is according to what intuition testifies, not according to what al-Nazzam claimed of the substantiality of his doctrine.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a lemma from al-Mawaqif regarding the implication of accident renewal for body renewal under al-Nazzam's doctrine. It begins by explaining the lemma: if the body is a collection of accidents (as al-Nazzam held), then the renewal of accidents necessarily entails the renewal of the body, because the body is nothing but those accidents. However, it notes an alternative from Sharh al-Tajrid: the Mu'tazila agreed that certain things (e.g., modes, beliefs, pains) are accidents not constitutive of the body, but colors, tastes, etc. were considered by al-Nazzam to be subtle bodies that aggregate to form dense bodies. The passage then discusses the phrase 'without need to extend the proof' (sard al-dalil). It explains that extending the proof means applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was originally established (here, accidents) due to some obscurity. It recounts that al-Nazzam extended the proof from accidents to bodies, claiming bodies also do not endure. Al-Amidi says this is because al-Nazzam's principle is that the substance (jawhar) is composed of accidents. So the renewal of accidents does not by itself negate the need to extend the proof. The passage then examines the condition 'if bodies are composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad)'. Despite this being famed as al-Nazzam's view, the commentator argues that for al-Nazzam even the individual atom is composed of mere aggregated accidents (as will be explained later). Therefore, the need for extending the proof is the same on both views (body as aggregate of accidents vs. body as composed of atoms) because the basis for negating the need is that a composite of mere accidents is itself an accident by intuition. So the proof of accident renewal automatically includes the body, and extension is unnecessary. The passage concludes that the lack of need is based on intuitive reason, not on al-Nazzam's claim of substantiality. It leaves open the possibility of another transmitted view (the part) but says the author did not mention it. The argument shows the theological subtlety of how different views of body composition affect the application of proofs.

Key Terms
عرض
جوهر
الجماد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All accidents are equally aspects of the body's reality.
Correction: Al-Nazzam, like other Mu'tazila, held that some accidents (e.g., modes, beliefs) do not enter into the body's reality, while others (colors, tastes) are considered subtle bodies.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nazzam, what are colors and tastes?
A) Accidents that have no entry in the body's reality
B) Substances (jawahir) or subtle bodies
C) Modes (akwan)
D) Individual atoms (jawahir afrad)

Key Takeaway
Al-Nazzam's doctrine that the body is an aggregate of accidents leads to the conclusion that accident renewal automatically entails body renewal, but this is based on his unique view of what constitutes a substance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your body is nothing but a collection of continuously renewing accidents, what part of 'you' remains constant? How does that affect your understanding of accountability for actions done in a body that is never the same from moment to moment? Will you now pay more attention to the intentions of your heart, which may not be subject to such renewal?
?
Al-Nazzam saw physical properties like colors and tastes as subtle bodies that interpenetrate. Do you view your own physical sensations as merely temporary or as part of your enduring self? How does this perspective influence the seriousness you give to physical worship acts like prayer or fasting? Commit to observing one physical act of worship this week with the awareness that it is composed of renewing accidents.
?
The lesson distinguishes between accidents that do not enter into the reality of the body and those that do (according to al-Nazzam). What in your life do you consider 'accidental' and 'essential' to your identity? Is there a trait you consider essential that might actually be accidental? Challenge yourself to ask whether your faith is an accident or substance in your life.

Logic and Technical Terms

The Concept of Extending the Proof (Sard al-Dalil)
Defines sard al-dalil and discusses its application in al-Nazzam's argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is meant by 'extending the proof' (sard al-dalil) in kalam reasoning and why al-Nazzam's extension from accidents to bodies is significant.

Core Idea
Extending the proof means applying a general proof to its particulars; al-Nazzam extended the accident proof to bodies.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of 'extending the proof' (sard al-dalil). The passage explains that when a proof is established for a general category, it may need to be extended to its particulars if there is obscurity. Al-Nazzam extended the proof of the non-endurance of accidents to bodies, claiming bodies also do not endure. This lesson unpacks that logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and find the definition of sard al-dalil
The passage says: 'perhaps the meaning of extending the proof is applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was established, due to obscurity therein.' Locate this definition.
This is a technical term in kalam.
2
Understand why al-Nazzam needed to extend it
Al-Nazzam took a proof that originally applied to accidents and argued that it also applies to bodies. Ask: what is his basis for this extension?
Refer to the previous lesson for his view on body composition.
3
Reflect on al-Amidi's comment
Al-Amidi notes that the extension is built on al-Nazzam's principle that the substance is composed of accidents. This means the extension is not automatic but requires justification.
Think about why al-Amidi says this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (يلزم من تجدد الأعراض تجدد (الأجسام لأنَّ المستفاد من قوله أن الجسم مجموع أعراض مجتمعة أنها باقية على عروضيتها وصارت بسبب الاجتماع أجساماً فيكون تجددها موجباً لتجددها هذا لكن في شرح التجريد أن المذكور في كتب المعتزلة أن مثل الأكوان والاعتقادات والآلام واللذات وما أشبه ذلك أعراض لا دخل لها في حقيقة الجسم وفاقاً وأما الألوان والطعوم والروائح والأصوات والكيفيات الملموسة من الحرارة والبرودة وغيرهما فعن النظام جواهر بل أجسام حيث صرح بأنَّ كلاً من ذلك لطيف مركب من جواهر مجتمعة ثم إنَّ تلك الأجسام اللطيفة إذا اجتمعت وتداخلت صارت الجسم الكثيف الذي هو الجماد . :قوله : ( بلا حاجة إلى طرد الدليل لعل المراد من طرد الدليل إجراؤها في جزئي من جزئيات ما أقيم عليه لخفاء فيه كما سيجيء في التنبيه المذكور في المقصد الثالث الأجسام باقية حيث قال : الدليل لما قام في الأعراض طرده النظام في الأجسام فقال بعدم بقائها أيضا قال الآمدي : وذلك لأنه مبني على أصله وهو أنَّ الجوهر مركب من الأعراض انتهى فعلى هذا لزوم تجدد الأجسام من تجدد الأعراض لا ينفي الاحتياج إلى الطرد. قوله : ( وإنما يحتاج إليه إذا كانت الأجسام عنده مركبة من الجواهر الأفراد فيه بحث لأن تركب الجسم من الجواهر الأفراد الغير المتناهية وإن كان مشهوراً من مذهبه إلا أن الجوهر الفرد بل الجوهر مطلقاً مركب عنده من محض الأعراض المجتمعة كما سيجيء في موقف الجوهر فالأجزاء الغير المتناهية عنده جواهر غير متناهية مركب كل منها من الأعراض المجتمعة ولا فرق في الاحتياج المذكور وعدمه بين القولين لأن مبنى نفي الاحتياج على تقدير كون الجسم مجموع الأعراض المجتمعة هو أنَّ المركب من محض الأعراض يلزم أن يكون عرضاً كما يشهد به البديهة وإن كان جوهراً عند النظام فالدليل الدال على تجدد الأعراض دال على تجدد الجسم لاندراجه فيها فلا احتياج إلى طرد الدليل فيه كما لا احتياج إلى طرده في خصوصيات الأعراض وهذا اللزوم لا يختلف على القولين كما لا يخفى على المتأمل اللهم إلا أن يثبت عنه نقل آخر وهو القول بالجزء على نحو ما قال به سائر المتكلمين، وإن لم يذكره المصنف وبما ذكرنا يظهر أن عدم الاحتياج إلى طرد الدليل على ما يشهد به البديهة لا على ما ادعاه النظام من جوهرية مذهبه
His statement: (It follows from the renewal of accidents the renewal of bodies) because what is understood from his statement that the body is a collection of accidents is that they (the accidents) remain upon their accidentally and by aggregation become bodies, so their renewal necessitates their renewal. However, in Sharh al-Tajrid it is mentioned that what is recorded in the books of the Mu'tazila is that things like modes (akwan), beliefs, pains, pleasures, and the like are accidents that have no entry in the reality of the body by agreement. As for colors, tastes, smells, sounds, and tangible qualities like heat and cold and others, according to al-Nazzam they are substances (jawahir) rather bodies (ajsam), for he explicitly stated that each of these is a subtle thing composed of aggregated substances, and then those subtle bodies when they aggregate and interpenetrate become the dense body which is the inanimate. His statement: (without need to extend the proof (sard al-dalil)) perhaps the meaning of 'extending the proof' is applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was established, due to obscurity therein, as will come in the notice mentioned in the third objective: bodies are enduring. For he said: The proof when it was established for accidents, al-Nazzam extended it to bodies and said they also do not endure. Al-Amidi said: That is because it is built upon his principle – that the substance (jawhar) is composed of accidents. End of quote. On this basis, the necessity of bodies' renewal from the renewal of accidents does not negate the need for extending the proof. His statement: (And it is only needed if bodies in his view are composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad).) There is discussion in it, because composition of the body from infinite individual atoms – though it is well-known from his doctrine – nevertheless the individual atom, nay substance absolutely, is in his view composed of mere aggregated accidents, as will come in the station of substance. So the infinite parts are in his view infinite substances each composed of aggregated accidents. There is no difference between the two views concerning the aforementioned need or lack thereof, because the basis for negating the need on the assumption that the body is a collection of aggregated accidents is that a composite of mere accidents necessarily is an accident, as intuition (badiha) testifies, even if it is a substance according to al-Nazzam. So the proof indicating the renewal of accidents indicates the renewal of the body because it falls under them, so there is no need to extend the proof to it, just as there is no need to extend it to specifics of accidents. And this implication does not differ between the two views, as is not hidden from the contemplator. Unless there is established from him another transmitted statement – namely the saying of the part (al-juz') in the manner spoken by the rest of the theologians, even if the author did not mention it. And by what we have mentioned it becomes apparent that the lack of need for extending the proof is according to what intuition testifies, not according to what al-Nazzam claimed of the substantiality of his doctrine.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a lemma from al-Mawaqif regarding the implication of accident renewal for body renewal under al-Nazzam's doctrine. It begins by explaining the lemma: if the body is a collection of accidents (as al-Nazzam held), then the renewal of accidents necessarily entails the renewal of the body, because the body is nothing but those accidents. However, it notes an alternative from Sharh al-Tajrid: the Mu'tazila agreed that certain things (e.g., modes, beliefs, pains) are accidents not constitutive of the body, but colors, tastes, etc. were considered by al-Nazzam to be subtle bodies that aggregate to form dense bodies. The passage then discusses the phrase 'without need to extend the proof' (sard al-dalil). It explains that extending the proof means applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was originally established (here, accidents) due to some obscurity. It recounts that al-Nazzam extended the proof from accidents to bodies, claiming bodies also do not endure. Al-Amidi says this is because al-Nazzam's principle is that the substance (jawhar) is composed of accidents. So the renewal of accidents does not by itself negate the need to extend the proof. The passage then examines the condition 'if bodies are composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad)'. Despite this being famed as al-Nazzam's view, the commentator argues that for al-Nazzam even the individual atom is composed of mere aggregated accidents (as will be explained later). Therefore, the need for extending the proof is the same on both views (body as aggregate of accidents vs. body as composed of atoms) because the basis for negating the need is that a composite of mere accidents is itself an accident by intuition. So the proof of accident renewal automatically includes the body, and extension is unnecessary. The passage concludes that the lack of need is based on intuitive reason, not on al-Nazzam's claim of substantiality. It leaves open the possibility of another transmitted view (the part) but says the author did not mention it. The argument shows the theological subtlety of how different views of body composition affect the application of proofs.

Key Terms
طرد الدليل
الآمدي
الجوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Extending the proof means applying the same conclusion to unrelated things.
Correction: Extending the proof means applying it to the particulars of the same category when there is obscurity.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'sard al-dalil' according to the passage?
A) Establishing a new proof for bodies
B) Applying the proof to its particulars due to obscurity
C) Denying the proof for accidents
D) Repeating the proof for emphasis

Key Takeaway
Sard al-dalil is the application of a proof to its particulars when there is obscurity; al-Nazzam extended the proof of accident renewal to bodies based on his principle that substance is composed of accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Nazzam extended a proof based on a principle he held without question. What principles do you rely on when applying Islamic teachings to modern issues? Have you ever examined whether those principles are truly from revelation or just inherited assumptions?
?
If the underlying principle is wrong, the whole extension collapses. Think of a belief you hold that you have never questioned. What would it take for you to re-examine it? Are you willing to test your foundations, or do you fear what you might find?
?
Al-Amidi pointed out that the necessity of renewal does not negate the need for extending the proof. Do you ever assume that something is automatically true without properly extending the evidence? When has that led you to a mistaken conclusion in your faith or life?

Individual Atoms and the Need for Proof Extension
Argues that al-Nazzam's atom view does not affect the need for proof extension, and concludes that the lack of need is based on intuition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nazzam's view on individual atoms (jawahir afrad) does not change the need to extend the proof, and the role of intuition in establishing the body's accidental nature.

Core Idea
Even if body is composed of atoms, each atom is still made of accidents, so body is accident by intuition.

This lesson tackles a discussion about whether the need to extend the proof changes if the body is composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad). The commentator argues that for al-Nazzam, even the individual atom is a composite of accidents, so the body is inevitably an accident by intuition. Thus, the proof for accident renewal automatically covers the body, and no extension is needed. The lesson also touches on a possible alternate transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two views
The passage considers both the view that body is an aggregate of accidents and the view that body is composed of individual atoms. Locate these two descriptions.
These are the two positions attributed to al-Nazzam.
2
Understand why they lead to the same conclusion
Even if the body is atoms, each atom is itself a composite of accidents. So a composite of mere accidents is necessarily an accident by intuition (badiha). Thus the proof for accidents includes the body.
This is the key argument.
3
Reflect on the role of intuition (badiha)
The passage emphasises that it is intuitive reason, not al-Nazzam's specific doctrine, that justifies the lack of need for extension. Ask yourself: What role does intuition play?
This anchors the argument in common reason.
4
Consider the exception
The passage mentions a possible alternate transmission where al-Nazzam might have held a different view about the part (al-juz'). Think about how this would affect the argument.
The commentator sets this aside as not mentioned by the author.

قوله : (يلزم من تجدد الأعراض تجدد (الأجسام لأنَّ المستفاد من قوله أن الجسم مجموع أعراض مجتمعة أنها باقية على عروضيتها وصارت بسبب الاجتماع أجساماً فيكون تجددها موجباً لتجددها هذا لكن في شرح التجريد أن المذكور في كتب المعتزلة أن مثل الأكوان والاعتقادات والآلام واللذات وما أشبه ذلك أعراض لا دخل لها في حقيقة الجسم وفاقاً وأما الألوان والطعوم والروائح والأصوات والكيفيات الملموسة من الحرارة والبرودة وغيرهما فعن النظام جواهر بل أجسام حيث صرح بأنَّ كلاً من ذلك لطيف مركب من جواهر مجتمعة ثم إنَّ تلك الأجسام اللطيفة إذا اجتمعت وتداخلت صارت الجسم الكثيف الذي هو الجماد . :قوله : ( بلا حاجة إلى طرد الدليل لعل المراد من طرد الدليل إجراؤها في جزئي من جزئيات ما أقيم عليه لخفاء فيه كما سيجيء في التنبيه المذكور في المقصد الثالث الأجسام باقية حيث قال : الدليل لما قام في الأعراض طرده النظام في الأجسام فقال بعدم بقائها أيضا قال الآمدي : وذلك لأنه مبني على أصله وهو أنَّ الجوهر مركب من الأعراض انتهى فعلى هذا لزوم تجدد الأجسام من تجدد الأعراض لا ينفي الاحتياج إلى الطرد. قوله : ( وإنما يحتاج إليه إذا كانت الأجسام عنده مركبة من الجواهر الأفراد فيه بحث لأن تركب الجسم من الجواهر الأفراد الغير المتناهية وإن كان مشهوراً من مذهبه إلا أن الجوهر الفرد بل الجوهر مطلقاً مركب عنده من محض الأعراض المجتمعة كما سيجيء في موقف الجوهر فالأجزاء الغير المتناهية عنده جواهر غير متناهية مركب كل منها من الأعراض المجتمعة ولا فرق في الاحتياج المذكور وعدمه بين القولين لأن مبنى نفي الاحتياج على تقدير كون الجسم مجموع الأعراض المجتمعة هو أنَّ المركب من محض الأعراض يلزم أن يكون عرضاً كما يشهد به البديهة وإن كان جوهراً عند النظام فالدليل الدال على تجدد الأعراض دال على تجدد الجسم لاندراجه فيها فلا احتياج إلى طرد الدليل فيه كما لا احتياج إلى طرده في خصوصيات الأعراض وهذا اللزوم لا يختلف على القولين كما لا يخفى على المتأمل اللهم إلا أن يثبت عنه نقل آخر وهو القول بالجزء على نحو ما قال به سائر المتكلمين، وإن لم يذكره المصنف وبما ذكرنا يظهر أن عدم الاحتياج إلى طرد الدليل على ما يشهد به البديهة لا على ما ادعاه النظام من جوهرية مذهبه
His statement: (It follows from the renewal of accidents the renewal of bodies) because what is understood from his statement that the body is a collection of accidents is that they (the accidents) remain upon their accidentally and by aggregation become bodies, so their renewal necessitates their renewal. However, in Sharh al-Tajrid it is mentioned that what is recorded in the books of the Mu'tazila is that things like modes (akwan), beliefs, pains, pleasures, and the like are accidents that have no entry in the reality of the body by agreement. As for colors, tastes, smells, sounds, and tangible qualities like heat and cold and others, according to al-Nazzam they are substances (jawahir) rather bodies (ajsam), for he explicitly stated that each of these is a subtle thing composed of aggregated substances, and then those subtle bodies when they aggregate and interpenetrate become the dense body which is the inanimate. His statement: (without need to extend the proof (sard al-dalil)) perhaps the meaning of 'extending the proof' is applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was established, due to obscurity therein, as will come in the notice mentioned in the third objective: bodies are enduring. For he said: The proof when it was established for accidents, al-Nazzam extended it to bodies and said they also do not endure. Al-Amidi said: That is because it is built upon his principle – that the substance (jawhar) is composed of accidents. End of quote. On this basis, the necessity of bodies' renewal from the renewal of accidents does not negate the need for extending the proof. His statement: (And it is only needed if bodies in his view are composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad).) There is discussion in it, because composition of the body from infinite individual atoms – though it is well-known from his doctrine – nevertheless the individual atom, nay substance absolutely, is in his view composed of mere aggregated accidents, as will come in the station of substance. So the infinite parts are in his view infinite substances each composed of aggregated accidents. There is no difference between the two views concerning the aforementioned need or lack thereof, because the basis for negating the need on the assumption that the body is a collection of aggregated accidents is that a composite of mere accidents necessarily is an accident, as intuition (badiha) testifies, even if it is a substance according to al-Nazzam. So the proof indicating the renewal of accidents indicates the renewal of the body because it falls under them, so there is no need to extend the proof to it, just as there is no need to extend it to specifics of accidents. And this implication does not differ between the two views, as is not hidden from the contemplator. Unless there is established from him another transmitted statement – namely the saying of the part (al-juz') in the manner spoken by the rest of the theologians, even if the author did not mention it. And by what we have mentioned it becomes apparent that the lack of need for extending the proof is according to what intuition testifies, not according to what al-Nazzam claimed of the substantiality of his doctrine.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a lemma from al-Mawaqif regarding the implication of accident renewal for body renewal under al-Nazzam's doctrine. It begins by explaining the lemma: if the body is a collection of accidents (as al-Nazzam held), then the renewal of accidents necessarily entails the renewal of the body, because the body is nothing but those accidents. However, it notes an alternative from Sharh al-Tajrid: the Mu'tazila agreed that certain things (e.g., modes, beliefs, pains) are accidents not constitutive of the body, but colors, tastes, etc. were considered by al-Nazzam to be subtle bodies that aggregate to form dense bodies. The passage then discusses the phrase 'without need to extend the proof' (sard al-dalil). It explains that extending the proof means applying it to the particulars of the things for which the proof was originally established (here, accidents) due to some obscurity. It recounts that al-Nazzam extended the proof from accidents to bodies, claiming bodies also do not endure. Al-Amidi says this is because al-Nazzam's principle is that the substance (jawhar) is composed of accidents. So the renewal of accidents does not by itself negate the need to extend the proof. The passage then examines the condition 'if bodies are composed of individual atoms (jawahir afrad)'. Despite this being famed as al-Nazzam's view, the commentator argues that for al-Nazzam even the individual atom is composed of mere aggregated accidents (as will be explained later). Therefore, the need for extending the proof is the same on both views (body as aggregate of accidents vs. body as composed of atoms) because the basis for negating the need is that a composite of mere accidents is itself an accident by intuition. So the proof of accident renewal automatically includes the body, and extension is unnecessary. The passage concludes that the lack of need is based on intuitive reason, not on al-Nazzam's claim of substantiality. It leaves open the possibility of another transmitted view (the part) but says the author did not mention it. The argument shows the theological subtlety of how different views of body composition affect the application of proofs.

Key Terms
الجواهر الأفراد
بديهة
الجزء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If body is composed of individual atoms, then the proof for accident renewal does not apply directly.
Correction: Even if body is composed of atoms, each atom is itself composed of accidents, so the body is still an accident by intuition, and the proof applies.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the composition of the body from individual atoms not change the need to extend the proof?
A) Because atoms are not made of accidents
B) Because the individual atom is already a substance
C) Because each atom is composed of mere aggregated accidents, so the body is an accident by intuition
D) Because al-Nazzam later retracted this view

Key Takeaway
The need to extend the proof is independent of whether the body is seen as an aggregate of accidents or as composed of atoms; the underlying reason is that the body is an accident by intuition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that even complex arguments about atomism do not change the intuitive truth that the body is an accident. Where in your life have you overcomplicated a simple truth that your intuition already knows? How can you rely more on your fitra (natural disposition) in matters of faith?
?
The commentator warns that unless al-Nazzam had another view, the argument stands on intuition. Are there areas of your belief where you cling to a scholar's unique opinion (like al-Nazzam's substantiality) even when the intuitive truth is clear? What might be the spiritual cost of such intellectual resistance?
?
You have just read a detailed theological discussion that ultimately points to the self-evident. How does this affect your view of the role of intellectual effort in religion? Will you now approach theological debates with more humility, knowing that the foundation is often simple intuition? What specific change will you make in how you engage with complex arguments?

Answering the Body Persistence Objection with Annihilation
Objection and answer about body persistence using annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazili concept of annihilation (al-fana') is used to answer the objection that bodies could serve as a counterexample to the argument for accident renewal.

Core Idea
The body's persistence is countered by an accident of annihilation contrary to endurance.

In this passage, we encounter a sophisticated dialectic: if the proof that accidents are renewed is extended to bodies, an opponent might argue that bodies themselves serve as a counterexample. The answer is that bodies may cease due to a special accident—annihilation (al-fana')—as held by the Mu'tazila. This lesson unpacks the objection and the two main answers given, including an important nuance about whether annihilation subsists in the body or is without location.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a feel for the argument. Notice the dialectical structure: objection, first answer, second answer, and a preferred solution.
2
Identify the objection (naqd)
The objection is that if the proof of accident renewal is extended to bodies, the opponent (who holds bodies endure) can use bodies as a counterexample. Understand why this is a problem.
The proof would be contradicted if bodies are not renewed.
3
Examine the first answer: annihilation as a subsisting accident
The first answer says that bodies may cease due to an accident contrary to endurance, created by Allah, that subsists in the body—like al-fana' according to the Mu'tazila. Note the example of annihilation.
4
Address the objection to the first answer
A potential objection arises: the Basran Mu'tazila hold that annihilation is an accident created without location, not subsisting in the perishing thing. Consider why this objection might undermine the first answer.
If fana' does not subsist in the body, how can it cause the body to cease?
5
Study the two responses: possibility and preference
Two responses are given: (1) it is possible that Allah creates fana' first in a location and then attaches it to what He wills to annihilate; (2) the better answer is to liken the accident to fana' merely in being contrary to endurance, setting aside the question of subsistence.
The second answer avoids the need to affirm subsistence and parallels the Mu'tazili concept more abstractly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤيد ما ذكرناه قوله ( ومنه ( أي ومن طرد هذا الدليل في الأجسام ( يعلم أنه يرد الأجسام نقضاً عليه ) أي على هذا الدليل عند القائل ببقاء الأجسام ( وقد يجاب عنه ) أي عن هذا النقض ( بأنه ( يعني الجسم بل الجوهر مطلقا (قد يزول لعرض يقوم به ) أي بخلق الله سبحانه عرضاً منافياً للبقاء فيقوم ذلك العرض بالجوهر فيزول ( كالفناء عند المعتزلة ) فإنه عندهم عرض إذا خلقه الله فنيت الجواهر كلها فإن قيل: المشهور عن المعتزلة البصرية أن الفناء عرض مضاد للبقاء يخلقه الله لا في محل فتفنى به الجواهر فلا يكون قائماً بالفاني كما ادعيتموه، أجيب : بأنه جاز أن يخلق أولاً في محل ثم يتعلق بمحل أراد الله إفناءه والأولى أن يقال : المقصود تشبيه ذلك العرض بالفناء على مذهبهم في مجرد كونه منافياً للبقاء وإن افترقا في أن أحدهما قائم بالمحل دون الآخر ( أو ) بأنه قد يزول الجوهر لعرض ) لا يخلقه الله فيه عندنا يريد

قوله : ( وإنما يحتاج إليه إذا كانت الأجسام إلخ) وما قيل : إِنَّ الجوهر الفرد عنده مركب من الأعراض فلا فرق بين القولين في عدم الحاجة إلى الطرد فوهم إذ النظام لا يقول بالجوهر الفرد، فضلا عن تركبه من الأعراض كيف والتركيب ينافي الفردية ؟ قال في شرح التجريد : إنه لما صرح بأنَّ في الجسم أجزاء غير متناهية موجودة بالفعل لزمه القول بالجزء؛ لأنه إذا كان كل انقسام ممكن في الجسم حاصلاً فيه بالفعل فما لا يكون حاصلاً في الجسم امتنع حصوله فيه فيكون أجزاؤه غير قابلة للانقسام. فقد وقع فيما كان هارباً عنه غير معترف به فمعنى قوله : مركبة من الجواهر الأفراد مركبة من الأجزاء التي هي الجواهر الأفراد في الواقع، لا أنه معترف به. قوله : ( ويؤيد ما ذكرناه إلخ ) فإن القائل ببقاء الأجسام، إنما يقول بتركبها من الجوهر الفرد. قوله : ( عرض إذا خلقه الله إلخ إما متعدد كما قال أبو علي : إنّه تعالى يخلق لكل جوهر فناء، وإما غير متعدد كما قال غيره : إن فناء واحداً يكفي لإفناء كل الأجسام . قوله : ( والأولى إلخ لأن ما ذكره أولاً مجرد جواز عقلي لم يثبت نقله منهم مع أنه على القول بعدم تعدده يلزم قيام عرض واحد بمحال كثيرة . قوله : ( أن يقال : المقصود إلخ) فحينئذ قوله عند المعتزلة متعلق بقوله كالفناء لا بقول قد يزول في الوجه الأول . المجموع، وإنما لم يجعل مبنى نفي الاحتياج المذكور إن تجدد الجزء يستلزم تجدد الكل وإن سلم جوهرية الكل كما يشعر به عبارة اللزوم؛ لأن فيه شائبة تعيين الطريق في إثبات تجدد الجسم فلا يكون قولاً معتداً به فتأمل قوله : ( أجيب بأنه جاز إلخ) هذا هو المعقول، إذ لو كان لا في محل دائماً لكان نسبته إلى جميع الجواهر على السواء، فزوال بعضها به دون آخر ترجیح مرجح لكن المفهوم من سياق الكلام أنه احتمال صرف ليس بمنقول عن المعتزلة ولهذا عدل عنه وقال : والأولى إلخ .

بلا
And what supports what we have mentioned is his statement (and from it) – i.e., from extending this proof to bodies – (it is known that it presents bodies as a counterexample (naqd) against it) – i.e., against this proof according to the one who holds the endurance of bodies. (And it may be answered) – i.e., about this counterexample – (that it – meaning the body, nay the substance absolutely – (may cease due to an accident subsisting in it) – i.e., by Allah the Exalted creating an accident contrary to endurance, and that accident subsists in the substance and so it ceases – (like al-fana' (annihilation) according to the Mu'tazila). For it is in their view an accident; when Allah creates it, all substances perish. And if it is said: The well-known from the Basran Mu'tazila is that al-fana' is an accident contrary to endurance, which Allah creates without location (la fi mahall), so by it substances perish, and thus it does not subsist in the perishing thing as you have claimed. It is answered: It is possible that He creates it first in a location and then it attaches to the location that Allah wills to annihilate. And it is better to say: The intent is to liken that accident to fana' according to their doctrine in the mere fact of being contrary to endurance, even if they differ in that one of them subsists in a location while the other does not. (or) that the substance may cease due to an accident that Allah does not create in it in our view – he intends.

His statement: (And it is only needed if bodies etc.) and what was said: that the individual atom is in his view composed of accidents, so there is no difference between the two views in the lack of need for extending the proof – is an error, for al-Nazzam does not affirm the individual atom, let alone its composition from accidents; how can composition be compatible with individuality? He said in Sharh al-Tajrid: Since he explicitly stated that in the body there are infinite parts existing in act, it necessitates his saying of the part (al-juz'); because if every possible division in the body is actually present in it, then what is not present in the body is impossible to obtain in it, so its parts are indivisible. So he fell into what he was fleeing from, without acknowledging it. Thus the meaning of his statement 'composed of individual atoms' is that it is composed of parts which are the individual atoms in reality, not that he acknowledges it. His statement: (And it supports what we have mentioned etc.) – for the one who affirms the endurance of bodies only affirms that they are composed of the individual atom. His statement: (an accident when Allah creates it etc.) – it is either multiple, as Abu Ali said: He the Exalted creates for each substance a fana', or it is not multiple, as others said: one single fana' suffices for the annihilation of all bodies. His statement: (And it is better etc.) – because what he mentioned first is merely an intellectual possibility whose transmission from them has not been established, especially since on the view of its non-multiplicity, it would entail one accident subsisting in many places. His statement: (that it is said: the intent etc.) – so in that case, his statement 'according to the Mu'tazila' is attached to his statement 'like al-fana'' not to the statement 'it may cease' in the first aspect. The sum: And he did not make the basis for the aforementioned negation of need that the renewal of the part necessitates the renewal of the whole even if the substantiality of the whole is conceded – as the phrasing of the implication suggests – because it has a tinge of specifying the path in proving the renewal of the body, so it is not a statement to be relied upon. So contemplate his statement: (It is answered that it is possible etc.) This is the intelligible, for if it were always without location, its relation to all substances would be equal, so its causing some to cease without others would be an unjustified preference. But what is understood from the context of speech is that it is a mere probability not transmitted from the Mu'tazila, and for this reason he turned away from it and said: 'And it is better etc.'

Without
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a combination of a main objection-and-answer section and several marginal glosses. It begins by supporting the previous argument with a statement: extending the proof to bodies allows the opponent (who holds bodies endure) to present bodies as a counterexample (naqd) against that proof. The answer is that bodies may cease due to an accident created by God that is contrary to endurance, similar to the Mu'tazili concept of annihilation (al-fana'). The passage then addresses a potential objection: the Basran Mu'tazila hold that fana' is an accident created without location, not subsisting in the perishing thing. The answer is that it is possible for God to first create it in a location and then attach it to what He wills to annihilate. The better answer is to liken the accident to fana' simply in being contrary to endurance, even if they differ in subsistence. Another possibility is that the substance may cease due to an accident not created in it (according to 'us'). The glosses then discuss various points: the error in claiming no difference between the two views on body composition because al-Nazzam does not affirm the individual atom; the implications of infinite parts in act for al-Nazzam's position; the interpretations of fana' being multiple or single; the preference for the intellectual possibility and its correction; the attachment of 'according to the Mu'tazila' to 'like al-fana''; and a final remark that the basis for negating the need for extending the proof should not be based on part-whole implication because it specifies the path. The passage ends with a note on the answer being a mere probability not transmitted from the Mu'tazila.

Key Terms
نقض (counterexample)
فناء (annihilation)
عرض (accident)
بقاء (endurance)
الموتزلة (Mu'tazila)
لا في محل (without location)
بصرية (Basran)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Mu'tazili concept of fana' must always be an accident without location, making it impossible for it to cause the cessation of a body by subsisting in it.
Correction: The passage shows that there are multiple interpretations; the preferred answer does not require fana' to subsist in the body, only that it be contrary to endurance.

Checkpoint
How is the objection that bodies present a counterexample (naqd) to the proof of accident renewal answered according to the passage?
A) Bodies are not subject to renewal at all.
B) Bodies may cease due to an accident created by God that is contrary to endurance, such as al-fana' according to the Mu'tazila.
C) The proof does not apply to bodies because they are substances.
D) The objection is invalid because bodies are composed of accidents.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili concept of annihilation (al-fana') provides a way to answer the objection of body persistence by introducing a special accident contrary to endurance, with the subtlety that it need not subsist in the body itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an intellectual objection to your faith that seems strong, do you, like the author of this passage, engage deeply with the objection and seek nuanced answers from within the tradition? Or do you avoid the discomfort? What is one specific objection you have confronted, and how have you responded?
?
The passage shows that even a seemingly solid argument (body persistence) can be answered by considering alternative possibilities (annihilation accident). In your life, when you encounter a situation that seems to contradict God's wisdom or mercy, do you actively seek out possible explanations from revelation and reason, or do you let the contradiction weaken your trust in Him? Commit to one practical step to increase your intellectual patience.
?
The scholars debated subtle points like whether an accident must subsist in a location. This requires humility before revelation. Are you willing to accept that some divine actions may transcend your neat categories? How does this lesson challenge your tendency to demand that God's ways fit your expectations?

The Accident Does Not Persist for Two Moments
Al-Jurjani states the objection that re-creation implies persistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core claim that an accident does not persist for two moments and the opponent's argument based on the possibility of re-creation.

Core Idea
Accidents cease to exist after one moment; they do not endure.

In this passage, al-Jurjani states the seventh objective: that the accident does not remain for two moments. He then presents a possible objection: if an accident can be re-created after non-existence, why cannot it simply persist? This objection sets up the debate about the nature of temporal existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the statement of the objective and the structure of the opponent's argument.
The opponent uses an a fortiori argument: if re-creation is possible, persistence is even more fitting.
2
Identify the opponent's reasoning
The opponent argues that since an accident can be re-created (i'ada) in a second time after non-existence, it should be even more possible for it to exist continuously (persist) without interruption.
This is based on the assumption that the two cases are analogous.
3
Understand key terms
Focus on 'accident' (عرض), 'persistence' (بقاء), 're-creation' (إعادة), and 'interpolation of non-existence' (تخلل العدم). These are central to the argument.
4
Reflect on the opponent's argument
Ask yourself: Is the analogy between re-creation and persistence valid? The next lesson will reveal the refutation.
This prepares you for the critical analysis.

المرصد الأول - المقصد السابع : أن العرض لا يبقي زمانين
لأن الموت كما هو المشهور عدم الحياة عن محل اتصف بها وإذا لم تكن الأجسام باقية كان محل الموت غير الجسم الموصوف بالحياة ( الثالث العرض يجوز إعادته وهو ) أي إعادته بتأويل أن يعاد ) وجوده في الوقت الثاني ( الذي هو بعد وقت عدمه الذي هو عقيب وقت وجوده ( وإذا جاز ) وجود العرض في وقتين ( مع تخلل العدم ) بينهما في وقت متوسط بين الوقتين ( فبدونه ) أي فوجوده بدون تخلل العدم بل على سبيل الاستمرار ( أولى ) بالجواز فلا يمتنع بقاء الأعراض ( قلنا : الشيخ منع إعادة العرض ولا ضير عليه في ذلك ( وإن سلم ( أن الإعادة جائزة ( فقياس بلا جامع) أي قياسكم وجوده في الوقتين بلا تخلل العدم على وجوده فيهما بدونه قياس لا جامع فيه ) ودعوى (الأولوية ) أي أولوية الوجود بلا تخلل العدم بالجواز ) دعوی بلا دليل) عليها لجواز أن يكون تخلل العدم شرطا للوجود في الوقت الثاني فيمكن الإعادة دون البقاء (بل) نقول : ( ذلك ) أعني الوجود في الوقتين مع تخلل العدم ( عندنا جائز وهذا أي الوجود فيهما بلا تخلله (ممتنع) فلا يصح قياس الثاني على الأول في الجواز أصلاً وقد يقال : كما أن الحكم ببقاء الأجسام ضروري يحكم به العقل بمعونته الحس
:قوله : ( كما هو المشهور إشارة إلى أنه لو فسر الموت بعدم الحياة عن مثل ما اتصف بالحياة يصح الحكم بالموت لكنه خلاف المشهور. قوله : ( بتأويل) إن التأويل لأجل تذكير الضمير فلا حاجة إليه ؛ لأنه لتذكير الخبر، ولأنَّ المصدر الذي لا يفرق بينه وبين مذكره بالتاء يجوز فيه التذكير والتأنيث وإن كان بواسطة حمل الوجود عليه فالإشكال باق لعدم صحة حمل الوجود على أن يعاد أيضاً حقيقة وطريق التسامح وسيع .
قوله : ( ولا ضير عليه لأنه لا يخل بحشر الأجساد إذ الأعراض لا تعاد أصلاً إنما الخلاف في أنه بجميع الأجزاء الأصلية وبإعادتها بعد الانعدام .
قوله : ( بتأويل أن يعاد المحوج إلى التأويل لفظي ومعنوي أما اللفظي فهو تذكير الضمير وأما المعنوي فلان الإعادة إيجاد لا وجود. قوله ( ولا ضير عليه في ذلك أي بحسب الشرع فإنَّ المنع المذكور لا ينافي القول الأجساد، لجواز أن يعاد الأجساد مع توارد الأمثال من الأعراض التي لا يمكن خلو الجواهر عنها على تلك الأجساد . بحشر
قوله : ( وهذا أي الوجود فيهما بلا تخلله ممتنع لأنه يلزم حينئذ قيام العرض، أعني البقاء ) بالعرض وقد مر بطلانه وأما أن تخلل العدم بين زماني وجود العرض فلا يلزم هذا المحذور هذا هو الفارق بين تجويز إعادة العرض مع تخلل العدم وعدم تجويز وجود في زمانين بدون ذلك التخلل وإن مر تضعيف هذا الفارق بمنع كون البقاء عرضاً .
The First Observation – The Seventh Objective: That the accident does not remain for two moments. Because death, as is well-known, is the non-existence of life from a locus that was qualified by it. And if bodies are not permanent, then the locus of death is other than the body described by life. (Third: It is permissible to recreate the accident, i.e., its re-creation by interpretation that it is re-created) its existence in the second time (which is after the time of its non-existence, which is immediately after the time of its existence. And if it is permissible) for the accident to exist in two times (with the interpolation of non-existence) between them in a time intermediate between the two times, then without it (i.e., its existence without the interpolation of non-existence, but rather by way of continuity) is more fitting (for permissibility), so the persistence of accidents is not impossible. (We said: The Shaykh prohibited the re-creation of the accident, and there is no harm upon him in that. And even if it is granted) that re-creation is permissible, (then it is an analogy without a common factor) i.e., your analogy of its existence in two times without interpolation of non-existence to its existence in two times with it is an analogy lacking a common factor. And the claim (of priority) i.e., the priority of existence without interpolation of non-existence in permissibility, is a claim without proof, because it is possible that the interpolation of non-existence is a condition for existence in the second time, so re-creation is possible without persistence. (Rather) we say: (That) i.e., existence in two times with interpolation of non-existence (is permissible according to us, and this) i.e., existence in them without interpolation (is impossible), so analogizing the second to the first in permissibility is not valid at all. And it is said: Just as the judgment of the persistence of bodies is necessary, the intellect judges it with the aid of sense. His statement: (As is well-known) is an indication that if death were interpreted as non-existence of life from something similar to what was qualified by life, the judgment of death would be valid, but it is contrary to the well-known. His statement: (By interpretation) The interpretation is for the purpose of making the pronoun masculine, so there is no need for it, because it is for making the predicate masculine, and because the verbal noun which is not distinguished from its masculine by the tā' allows both masculine and feminine, even if it is by way of attributing existence to it, the problem remains due to the invalidity of attributing existence to 'that it is re-created' also in reality, and the way of tolerance is broad. His statement: (And there is no harm upon him) because it does not invalidate the resurrection of bodies, since accidents are not re-created at all; the dispute is only about whether it is with all the original parts and by their re-creation after annihilation. His statement: (By interpretation that it be re-created) The need for interpretation is verbal and conceptual: as for the verbal, it is making the pronoun masculine; as for the conceptual, because re-creation is bringing into existence, not existence. His statement: (And there is no harm upon him in that) i.e., according to the Law, for the mentioned prohibition does not contradict the statement of the resurrection of bodies, because it is permissible that bodies be re-created with the succession of similar accidents which cannot be devoid of substances upon those bodies. His statement: (And this) i.e., existence in them without its interpolation (is impossible) because it would necessitate then the subsistence of the accident, namely persistence, by an accident, and its invalidity has already passed. As for the interpolation of non-existence between the two times of the existence of the accident, this danger does not arise. This is the difference between permitting the re-creation of the accident with interpolation of non-existence and not permitting existence in two times without that interpolation, though the weakening of this difference by denying that persistence is an accident has passed.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an argument about whether an accident can persist for two moments, followed by commentary. The author (al-Jurjani) begins by stating the seventh objective: that the accident does not remain for two moments. He then presents a hypothetical objection: an opponent might argue that since it is possible to recreate an accident after its non-existence (i.e., bring it back into existence in a second time after it has ceased), then continuous existence (persistence) without the interpolation of non-existence should be even more permissible, so the persistence of accidents is not impossible. The author responds in several steps: First, the Shaykh (al-Iji) prohibits the re-creation of accidents, and this does not harm his position regarding the resurrection of bodies because accidents are not re-created anyway; only bodies are re-created, with new accidents succeeding each other. Second, even if re-creation is granted, the opponent's analogy is invalid because it lacks a common factor: the case of existence with interpolation is different from existence without interpolation, as the interpolation may be a condition for the second existence. Third, the claim that existence without interpolation is more fitting for permissibility is unproven; it could be that the interpolation is a necessary condition. Fourth, the author states that in his school, existence with interpolation is permissible, but existence without it is impossible, so analogy fails. Finally, there is a remark that just as the persistence of bodies is known by necessity with sensory aid, the same may be true for accidents, though this is not elaborated. The subsequent glosses explain specific terms: the definition of death, the reason for interpretation of the pronoun, that the prohibition does not affect the resurrection doctrine, and that the impossibility of continuous existence without interpolation stems from the fact that persistence would then be an accident subsisting by an accident, which is invalid; whereas interpolation avoids this.

بقاء
إعادة
تخلل العدم
زمان

C) Bodies persist, so accidents must also persist.
D) The intellect cannot judge persistence.

The opponent argues that if an accident can be re-created after non-existence, continuous persistence should be even more permissible.

Does this reasoning resonate with you? Reflect on your own life: do you assume that because something good happened once, it should persist forever? ?

Have you ever held a belief about Allah or His creation that felt 'logical' but turned out to be contrary to what the scholars teach? Logic and Technical Terms

5 min
Refuting the Analogy: Re-creation vs. Persistence
Al-Jurjani refutes the opponent's analogy and explains the difference between re-creation and persistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the analogy between re-creation and persistence fails, and the role of interpolation of non-existence.

Core Idea
Re-creation with interpolation is different from persistence without it.

In this response, al-Jurjani refutes the opponent's analogy. He first notes that the Shaykh prohibits re-creation of accidents, but even if it were granted, the analogy lacks a common factor because the interpolation of non-existence may be a condition for re-creation. Thus, the two cases are not comparable.

Guided Path
1
Read the response passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the refutation. Notice the three parts: reference to the Shaykh's prohibition, the invalidity of the analogy, and the claim of priority being unproven.
The author uses a logical critique: the analogy lacks a common factor (جامع).
2
Understand the concept of interpolation
Interpolation of non-existence (تخلل العدم) is the period of non-existence between two moments of existence. The author argues that this may be a necessary condition for existence in the second time.
Without this condition, the cases are fundamentally different.
3
Analyze the refutation
The author first mentions the Shaykh's prohibition to show that re-creation is not universally accepted. Then, even granting re-creation, the analogy fails. The claim that existence without interpolation is more fitting is unsupported.
The conclusion: existence with interpolation is permissible, without it is impossible.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider why the interpolation of non-existence changes the case. It may be that an accident cannot exist in two contiguous moments without a break.
This is a key theological point in kalam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Re-creation and persistence are essentially the same thing.
Correction: They are different because re-creation involves a period of non-existence, which may be a necessary condition for existence in a second time.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Jurjani reject the analogy between re-creation and persistence?
A) Because re-creation is absolutely prohibited.
B) Because the analogy lacks a common factor; interpolation of non-existence may be a condition.
C) Because the intellect cannot compare the two cases.
D) Because the Shaykh's opinion is not authoritative.

Key Takeaway
The interpolation of non-existence breaks the analogy, making re-creation permissible but persistence impossible.

Defending the Doctrine: Resurrection and the Necessity of Bodies
Al-Jurjani explains the compatibility with resurrection and the necessity of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how denying the persistence of accidents does not contradict the resurrection of bodies, and why bodies must persist.

Core Idea
Accidents are not re-created at resurrection; bodies are re-created with new accidents.

In the final part of the passage, al-Jurjani addresses a potential concern: if accidents do not persist, how can bodies be resurrected? He explains that the resurrection concerns the bodies themselves, not the accidents, which are re-created anew. Moreover, the persistence of bodies is known by necessity, while accidents are not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on resurrection and necessity
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the claim that the judgment of persistence of bodies is necessary (ضروري) with sensory aid.
This distinguishes bodies from accidents.
2
Understand the glosses
The subsequent commentary explains specific points: definition of death, interpretation of pronoun, harmlessness of prohibition for resurrection, and the difference between cases.
Each gloss clarifies a potential misunderstanding.
3
Grasp the key distinction
Bodies persist necessarily; accidents do not. At resurrection, bodies are re-created with new accidents, not by re-creating the old accidents.
This is why denying persistence of accidents does not affect resurrection.
4
Reflect on the philosophical point
The impossibility of persistence without interpolation is due to the accident of persistence (بقاء) itself being an accident that would need to subsist by another accident, leading to infinite regress.
This is a technical argument in kalam.

المرصد الأول - المقصد السابع : أن العرض لا يبقي زمانين
لأن الموت كما هو المشهور عدم الحياة عن محل اتصف بها وإذا لم تكن الأجسام باقية كان محل الموت غير الجسم الموصوف بالحياة ( الثالث العرض يجوز إعادته وهو ) أي إعادته بتأويل أن يعاد ) وجوده في الوقت الثاني ( الذي هو بعد وقت عدمه الذي هو عقيب وقت وجوده ( وإذا جاز ) وجود العرض في وقتين ( مع تخلل العدم ) بينهما في وقت متوسط بين الوقتين ( فبدونه ) أي فوجوده بدون تخلل العدم بل على سبيل الاستمرار ( أولى ) بالجواز فلا يمتنع بقاء الأعراض ( قلنا : الشيخ منع إعادة العرض ولا ضير عليه في ذلك ( وإن سلم ( أن الإعادة جائزة ( فقياس بلا جامع) أي قياسكم وجوده في الوقتين بلا تخلل العدم على وجوده فيهما بدونه قياس لا جامع فيه ) ودعوى (الأولوية ) أي أولوية الوجود بلا تخلل العدم بالجواز ) دعوی بلا دليل) عليها لجواز أن يكون تخلل العدم شرطا للوجود في الوقت الثاني فيمكن الإعادة دون البقاء (بل) نقول : ( ذلك ) أعني الوجود في الوقتين مع تخلل العدم ( عندنا جائز وهذا أي الوجود فيهما بلا تخلله (ممتنع) فلا يصح قياس الثاني على الأول في الجواز أصلاً وقد يقال : كما أن الحكم ببقاء الأجسام ضروري يحكم به العقل بمعونته الحس
:قوله : ( كما هو المشهور إشارة إلى أنه لو فسر الموت بعدم الحياة عن مثل ما اتصف بالحياة يصح الحكم بالموت لكنه خلاف المشهور. قوله : ( بتأويل) إن التأويل لأجل تذكير الضمير فلا حاجة إليه ؛ لأنه لتذكير الخبر، ولأنَّ المصدر الذي لا يفرق بينه وبين مذكره بالتاء يجوز فيه التذكير والتأنيث وإن كان بواسطة حمل الوجود عليه فالإشكال باق لعدم صحة حمل الوجود على أن يعاد أيضاً حقيقة وطريق التسامح وسيع .
قوله : ( ولا ضير عليه لأنه لا يخل بحشر الأجساد إذ الأعراض لا تعاد أصلاً إنما الخلاف في أنه بجميع الأجزاء الأصلية وبإعادتها بعد الانعدام .
قوله : ( بتأويل أن يعاد المحوج إلى التأويل لفظي ومعنوي أما اللفظي فهو تذكير الضمير وأما المعنوي فلان الإعادة إيجاد لا وجود. قوله ( ولا ضير عليه في ذلك أي بحسب الشرع فإنَّ المنع المذكور لا ينافي القول الأجساد، لجواز أن يعاد الأجساد مع توارد الأمثال من الأعراض التي لا يمكن خلو الجواهر عنها على تلك الأجساد . بحشر
قوله : ( وهذا أي الوجود فيهما بلا تخلله ممتنع لأنه يلزم حينئذ قيام العرض، أعني البقاء ) بالعرض وقد مر بطلانه وأما أن تخلل العدم بين زماني وجود العرض فلا يلزم هذا المحذور هذا هو الفارق بين تجويز إعادة العرض مع تخلل العدم وعدم تجويز وجود في زمانين بدون ذلك التخلل وإن مر تضعيف هذا الفارق بمنع كون البقاء عرضاً .
The First Observation – The Seventh Objective: That the accident does not remain for two moments. Because death, as is well-known, is the non-existence of life from a locus that was qualified by it. And if bodies are not permanent, then the locus of death is other than the body described by life. (Third: It is permissible to recreate the accident, i.e., its re-creation by interpretation that it is re-created) its existence in the second time (which is after the time of its non-existence, which is immediately after the time of its existence. And if it is permissible) for the accident to exist in two times (with the interpolation of non-existence) between them in a time intermediate between the two times, then without it (i.e., its existence without the interpolation of non-existence, but rather by way of continuity) is more fitting (for permissibility), so the persistence of accidents is not impossible. (We said: The Shaykh prohibited the re-creation of the accident, and there is no harm upon him in that. And even if it is granted) that re-creation is permissible, (then it is an analogy without a common factor) i.e., your analogy of its existence in two times without interpolation of non-existence to its existence in two times with it is an analogy lacking a common factor. And the claim (of priority) i.e., the priority of existence without interpolation of non-existence in permissibility, is a claim without proof, because it is possible that the interpolation of non-existence is a condition for existence in the second time, so re-creation is possible without persistence. (Rather) we say: (That) i.e., existence in two times with interpolation of non-existence (is permissible according to us, and this) i.e., existence in them without interpolation (is impossible), so analogizing the second to the first in permissibility is not valid at all. And it is said: Just as the judgment of the persistence of bodies is necessary, the intellect judges it with the aid of sense. His statement: (As is well-known) is an indication that if death were interpreted as non-existence of life from something similar to what was qualified by life, the judgment of death would be valid, but it is contrary to the well-known. His statement: (By interpretation) The interpretation is for the purpose of making the pronoun masculine, so there is no need for it, because it is for making the predicate masculine, and because the verbal noun which is not distinguished from its masculine by the tā' allows both masculine and feminine, even if it is by way of attributing existence to it, the problem remains due to the invalidity of attributing existence to 'that it is re-created' also in reality, and the way of tolerance is broad. His statement: (And there is no harm upon him) because it does not invalidate the resurrection of bodies, since accidents are not re-created at all; the dispute is only about whether it is with all the original parts and by their re-creation after annihilation. His statement: (By interpretation that it be re-created) The need for interpretation is verbal and conceptual: as for the verbal, it is making the pronoun masculine; as for the conceptual, because re-creation is bringing into existence, not existence. His statement: (And there is no harm upon him in that) i.e., according to the Law, for the mentioned prohibition does not contradict the statement of the resurrection of bodies, because it is permissible that bodies be re-created with the succession of similar accidents which cannot be devoid of substances upon those bodies. His statement: (And this) i.e., existence in them without its interpolation (is impossible) because it would necessitate then the subsistence of the accident, namely persistence, by an accident, and its invalidity has already passed. As for the interpolation of non-existence between the two times of the existence of the accident, this danger does not arise. This is the difference between permitting the re-creation of the accident with interpolation of non-existence and not permitting existence in two times without that interpolation, though the weakening of this difference by denying that persistence is an accident has passed.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an argument about whether an accident can persist for two moments, followed by commentary. The author (al-Jurjani) begins by stating the seventh objective: that the accident does not remain for two moments. He then presents a hypothetical objection: an opponent might argue that since it is possible to recreate an accident after its non-existence (i.e., bring it back into existence in a second time after it has ceased), then continuous existence (persistence) without the interpolation of non-existence should be even more permissible, so the persistence of accidents is not impossible. The author responds in several steps: First, the Shaykh (al-Iji) prohibits the re-creation of accidents, and this does not harm his position regarding the resurrection of bodies because accidents are not re-created anyway; only bodies are re-created, with new accidents succeeding each other. Second, even if re-creation is granted, the opponent's analogy is invalid because it lacks a common factor: the case of existence with interpolation is different from existence without interpolation, as the interpolation may be a condition for the second existence. Third, the claim that existence without interpolation is more fitting for permissibility is unproven; it could be that the interpolation is a necessary condition. Fourth, the author states that in his school, existence with interpolation is permissible, but existence without it is impossible, so analogy fails. Finally, there is a remark that just as the persistence of bodies is known by necessity with sensory aid, the same may be true for accidents, though this is not elaborated. The subsequent glosses explain specific terms: the definition of death, the reason for interpretation of the pronoun, that the prohibition does not affect the resurrection doctrine, and that the impossibility of continuous existence without interpolation stems from the fact that persistence would then be an accident subsisting by an accident, which is invalid; whereas interpolation avoids this.

بقاء
إعادة
حشر الأجساد

A) Because accidents are necessary for life.
B) Because accidents are not re-created at all; only bodies are re-created with new accidents.
C) Because the Shaykh allowed resurrection of accidents.

Key Takeaway
Bodies persist necessarily; accidents are re-created at each moment, including at resurrection, so the denial of accident persistence does not affect resurrection.

?
This lesson distinguishes between the persistence of your essential self (body) and the constant renewal of accidents (thoughts, moods). Have you ever considered that your changing emotions are temporary accidents, while your core self remains? How does that change how you view your sins and repentance?
?
