قوله : ( وهو حشو ما بين السطوح هكذا في موضع من الشفاء وفي موضع آخر ويقل عمق للشخن الذي يحصره السطوح فالمراد بالحشو ما يحشى به وإضافة الحشو إلى ما لامية كما هو الظاهر أي حشو خلاء متوهم بين السطوح، وما قيل : إن كلمة ما إبهامية وموصولة وإضافة الحشو إليه بيانية فتوجيه حشو . قوله : (الذي يحصره سطح واحد كالكرة المصمتة أشار به إلى أن ذكر السطح بطريق التمثيل إذ ليس المقصود بيان حد جامع مانع بل مجرد الإطلاق على المعاني . قوله : ( ويقل الطول إلخ ) لم يجمعها مع المعاني السابقة إشارة إلى كثرة الإطلاقات الأول. قوله : (من مركز العالم إلى محيطه كطول الإنسان وهو البعد الذي فيه أول حركة النشو كذا في الشفاء .
قوله : ( إلى الأرض أي إلى أسفله الذي في جانب الأرض . قوله : ( الامتداد الواحد الذي هو الخط صرح هاهنا بأن المعنى الأول هو نفس الخط ويدل
قوله : ( حشو ما بين السطوح أعني الجسم التعليمي إلخ) عبارة المتن لما لم يكن بحسب الظاهر متناولاً للجسم التعليمي الذي في الكرة المصمتة فإن فيها سطحاً واحداً لا سطوحاً ومتناولاً للجسم الطبيعي فسرها الشارح تصريحاً بالمقصود وإن كان أخذه من عبارة المصنف تعسفاً ولو بدل أعني بيعني لكان أظهر ثم إنَّ ما في قوله حشو ما بين السطوح إما مشددة إبهامية أو موصولة وإضافة الحشو إليه بيانية، وعلى التقديرين ليس المراد بالحشو المعنى المصدري ولا الحاصل به كما ظن ، بل المحشوبة إما اصطلاحاً أو المجاز اللغوي.

المرصد الثاني - المقصد الثالث : الأبعاد الثلاثة للجسم
C
الذي هو الجسم التعليمي ( ومنها ما هي كميات ) مأخوذة ( مع إضافة ) إلى أمر آخر ( كالمفروض ثانياً ) أو أولاً أو ثالثاً فإن كون الامتداد مفروضاً ثانياً إضافة له إلى المفروض أولاً وبالعكس وكونه مفروضاً ثالثاً إضافة إلى مجموع الأولين؛ كما أنَّ لمجموعهما أيضاً إضافة إليه ) وقد يعتبر معه ) أي مع الكم (إضافة ثالثة كالأطول ) فإنه أطول بالقياس إلى ما هو طويل مقيساً إلى قصير فهاهنا إضافتان الأطولية والطول المضايف للقصر لكنه عبر عن الأطولية بالإضافة الثالثة لأنها عارضة الأمر ثالث بعد أمرين تحقق بينهما الطول، أو لأنه نظر إلى أن القصر أيضاً إضافة مقابلة للطول وفيه بعد لأن القصر ليس مأخوذاً مع الأطول، ولو عبر عنها بالإضافة الثانية، لكان أظهر ( أو ) إضافة ( رابعة كالأطول بالنسبة إلى الغير الأطول بالقياس إلى آخر فيكون هناك ثلاث إضافات أطوليتان وطول إضافي . والأطولية الأولى عارضة لأمر رابع فجعلها إضافة رابعة على قياس ما مر، وجعلها ثالثة أولى وفي المباحث المشرقية أن هذه الكميات إذا أخذت مضافة إلى شيء فقد تؤخذ تارة بحيث لا يكون من شرط إضافتها إلى ذلك الشيء إضافتها إلى شيء آخر. وقد تؤخذ تارة أخرى بحيث يكون من شرط إضافتها إلى شيء إضافتها إلى شيء ثالث . مثال الأول أن يقال : هذا الخط طويل عندما يقال :
عليه قوله أي في نفسه بعد وامتداد واحد ، فالظاهر أن يقول : إن كل خط في نفسه طول كما وقع في التجريد الخط طول بلا عرض ولعله أراد بالطويل الطول لأنه متصف بالطول بمعنی دارز شدن وإن كان عينه بمعنى درازي وهذا المتمحل وإن صح إطلاق الطويل عليه لكن لا يصحح قوله وبهذا المعنى الخ لأنه بهذا المعنى قيل : كل خط طول ولا يجري في قوله : كل سطح عريض وكل جسم عميق .
قوله : ( وفي المباحث المشرقية الخ) تأييد لما ذكره سابقاً من أن في الأطول بالقياس إلى الطويل إضافتين وبالقياس إلى غير الأطول ثلاث إضافات .
(
قوله : ( كما أن لمجموعها أيضاً إضافة إليه تحقق الأول والثاني، وإن كان لا يستلزم تحقق الثالث ولا تعقله إلا أن الكلام في الأبعاد الجسمية فلذا كان للأولين إضافة إلى الثالث فإن تعين الطويل والعرض باعتبار العمق .
قوله : ( ولو عبر عنها بالإضافة الثانية لكان أظهر فإن قلت الأطول الذي ذكره المصنف من الطول بمعني أطول الامتدادين، ففيه زيادتان وطول هو إضافة أيضاً، فيصح القول بان الأطول اعتبر فيه إضافة ثالثة بلا تكلف قلت الطول المذكور بمعنى الامتداد مطلقاً وليس إضافة، والأقرب في توجيه كلام المصنف أن يقال : الأطول من زاد طوله على طول غيره بالنسبة إلى قصير ففيه الطولان الإضافيان والزيادة الإضافية فلا غبار في الكلام.
Second observation - Third purpose: The three dimensions of the body. It is said for thickness: it is the filling between surfaces, meaning the mathematical body which is enclosed by one surface or two surfaces or surfaces without additional condition, and in this sense it is said: if a body, then it is in itself deep. And it is said for descending thickness, i.e., thickness qualified by descent, and it is then called ascending thickness, i.e., qualified by ascent, thickness, and in this regard it is said: depth of the well and thickness of the minaret. And it is said: length and width and depth have other meanings besides what was mentioned, such as it is said: length is the extension extending from the center of the world to its circumference, which is the fourth of the meanings of length. And it is said: length also is the extension extending from a human's head to his feet and from the head of quadrupeds to their rear, and this is its meaning. And it is said: width is the extension from a human's right or quadrupeds' right to their left, which is the fourth of the meanings of width. And it is said: depth is the extension from a human's chest to his back and from the back of quadrupeds to the ground, and this is the fourth of the meanings of depth. And know that these mentioned meanings of length, width, and depth are some pure quantities, like length in the sense of the single extension which is the line, width in the sense of the surface, and depth in the sense of thickness. His saying: 'It is the filling between surfaces' thus in a place in the Shifa and in another place it is said depth for the thickness that the surfaces enclose, the intended meaning of 'filling' is that with which it is filled, and the addition of 'filling' to 'what' is lamiyya as is apparent, i.e., filling of an imagined void between surfaces. And it is said that the word 'what' is indefinite and relative, and the addition of 'filling' to it is explicative, thus directing 'filling'. His saying: 'which is enclosed by one surface' like the solid sphere, he indicated by this that mentioning surface as an example, since the intention is not to give a comprehensive and exclusive definition but only a general application to the meanings. His saying: 'and it is said length etc.' he did not combine them with the previous meanings, indicating the abundance of the first applications. His saying: 'from the center of the world to its circumference' like the length of a human, which is the dimension in which the first movement of growth occurs, thus in the Shifa. His saying: 'to the ground' i.e., to its lower part which is on the side of the ground. His saying: 'the single extension which is the line' he states here that the first meaning is the line itself, and it indicates. His saying: 'filling between surfaces meaning the mathematical body etc.' The expression of the text, since it apparently does not include the mathematical body that is in the solid sphere, for it has one surface not multiple surfaces, and includes the natural body, the commentator interpreted it explicitly as intended, although his taking it from the author's phrase is strained. And if he had replaced 'meaning' with 'i.e.', it would be clearer. Then what is in his saying 'filling between surfaces' is either an intensified indefinite or a relative, and the addition of 'filling' to it is explicative. In both cases the intended meaning of 'filling' is not the verbal noun nor the product as thought, but rather the filled thing either terminologically or as a linguistic metaphor. [PAGE_068] Second observation - Third purpose: The three dimensions of the body. C which is the mathematical body. And among them are quantities taken with addition to another matter, like the second assumed or first or third: for the extension being assumed second is an addition to the first assumed and vice versa, and being assumed third is an addition to the sum of the first two; just as the sum also has an addition to it. And sometimes a third addition is considered with it (i.e., with the quantity), like 'longer' (al-atwal): for it is longer in relation to what is long measured against a short one, so here there are two additions: the longer-ness and the length that is relative to shortness. But he expressed the longer-ness as the third addition because it is accidental to a third matter after two matters between which length is realized, or because he considered that shortness is also an addition opposite to length. But there is distance because shortness is not taken with the longer. And if he had expressed it as the second addition, it would be clearer. Or a fourth addition, like 'longer' in relation to another 'longer' in relation to yet another, so there are three additions: two longer-nesses and one relative length. The first longer-ness is accidental to a fourth matter, so he made it a fourth addition by analogy to what preceded, but making it third is preferable. And in the Eastern Investigations, these quantities when taken as added to something, they are sometimes taken such that it is not a condition of their addition to that thing that they be added to something else. And sometimes they are taken such that it is a condition of their addition to something that they be added to a third thing. Example of the first: it is said this line is long when it is said: upon it his saying: i.e., in itself dimension and single extension. So the apparent is that he should say: every line is in itself length, as occurred in the Tajrid: the line is length without width. Perhaps he intended by 'long' (tawil) length (tul), because it is qualified by length in the sense of 'having length' even if it is the same as 'length' in the sense of 'extension'. And this strained interpretation, even if it validates applying 'long' to it, does not validate his saying 'and in this sense etc.' because in this sense it is said: every line is length, and it does not apply in his saying: every surface is wide and every body is deep. His saying: 'and in the Eastern Investigations etc.' supports what he mentioned previously: that in 'longer' in relation to 'long' there are two additions, and in relation to other than 'longer' there are three additions. His saying: 'just as for their sum also there is an addition to it' realizes the first and second, although it does not necessitate realizing the third nor conceiving it, except that the discourse is about bodily dimensions, so for the first two there is an addition to the third, for length and width are determined by depth. His saying: 'and if he had expressed it as the second addition it would be clearer' then if you say: the 'longer' that the author mentioned is from length in the sense of the longer of two extensions, so it has two increases and length is also an addition, so it is correct to say that in 'longer' a third addition is considered without strain. I say: the mentioned length is in the sense of extension absolutely and is not an addition. The closest in directing the author's words is to say: 'longer' is he whose length increased over another's length in relation to a short one, so in it there are two relative lengths and a relative increase, so there is no flaw in the speech.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the three dimensions (length, width, depth) in multiple senses, followed by commentary. The text first defines thickness (thikhn) as the filling between surfaces, i.e., the mathematical body enclosed by one or more surfaces. It notes that in this sense, any body is deep in itself. It then distinguishes between descending thickness (depth of a well) and ascending thickness (thickness of a minaret). Next, it lists four meanings for each dimension: length as (1) the single extension (line), (2) from center of world to circumferences, (3) from head to foot of humans or animals, (4) the extension from right to left? Actually the fourth meaning of length is from center of world to circumference. The text then clarifies that some of these meanings are pure quantities (e.g., length as line, width as surface, depth as thickness) while others involve addition (e.g., specific orientations). The commentary on 'filling between surfaces' explains that 'filling' (hashw) refers to what fills, and the phrase is interpreted as either indefinite or relative, with an explicative addition. It notes that the example of a single surface (solid sphere) is illustrative, not a strict definition. The commentary also discusses the mathematical vs. natural body and the strained interpretation of the author's phrase. On page 68, the commentary continues with how these quantities are taken with addition, e.g., the 'longer' (atwal) involves two or three additions depending on relativity. It cites the Eastern Investigations on conditionality of addition. The discussion ends with clarification that 'longer' means one whose length exceeds another relative to a short one, involving two relative lengths and a relative increase.

Key Terms
طول (tul - length)
عرض (ard - width)
عمق (umq - depth)
امتداد (imtidad - extension)
إضافة (idafa - addition/relation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which dimension has a meaning involving 'from the center of the world to its circumference'?
A) Width
B) Depth
C) Length
D) Thickness

Key Takeaway
Length, width, and depth each have multiple meanings, including astronomical and anatomical senses, beyond their pure quantitative definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a single physical dimension like length can have multiple valid meanings (line, astronomical, anatomical), how does that challenge your assumption that theological terms have only one straightforward definition? What might you need to re-examine?
?
The passage distinguishes between 'pure quantities' and relational extensions. Think of a concept in your own life (e.g., 'success', 'love', 'justice') that you have treated as a pure quantity. How would your understanding change if you considered its relational meanings as equally valid?
?
When you encounter a difficult term in Islamic texts, do you tend to settle for one meaning or actively explore multiple dimensions? What is one term you could study more deeply this week, inspired by this lesson's approach?
